Action: FYI
Following is a translation of a report subritted by AMMUG-1
concerning a shipment of explosives to Mexico:
"The Communist Party of El Salvador had asked me
to send them twenty-five one-quarter pound packages of
gelatin explosives. They requested that the explosives
be sent to Mexico where they would recover them and take
them to El Salvador.
Manuel PINEIRO
'In view of the request, I spoke wit
regarding the shipment itself, as well as the amount.
PIÑEIRO answered by telling me to do so.
me
During my trip to Mexico (March 1954, I spoke with
Rogelic RODRIGUEZ Lopez regarding this heat and he
told that there was no need of my sending the explosives
to Mexico as this type of explosive was ailable in the
Embassy. I then told RODRIGUEZ that I world answer the
request from El Salvador.
*Upon returning to Cuba I spoke with "INEIRO, who
told me not to send the explosives as the orders now were
to send nothing but money due to the recent exposure of
the arms shipment to Venezuela.
Distribution:
2. - COS, Mexico City
Chester D. DAINOLD

6. L-9 revealed that he had welcomed in the New Year at Nico GARCIA's
hame at Nico's invitation. When Nico picked him up at the Embassy they
made a swing by a house at 131 Alofaniro Duras, Polanco, where fico wanted
to drop a couple of bottles off with a friend nanod Mary, a Cuban. L-9 tried
but Nico insisted that
to remain in the car -- was not dressed for calling
he come in. Mary was not there but her sister was she had just recently
anti-Castro
arrived from Cuba. Another Cuban man and woman were there
- the man was
types who were very sad at being away from their honaland
L-9 says
softly crying -- probably a bit liquored up. Nice fit right in
that he is a master at getting along with people, even those on the other side
of the political fence. (This tallies with info on file). The Mexican landlady.
an old crone tried to put the make on L-9, really flipped for him, and
wanted him to stay but he and Hico finally drove off. L-9 does not know who
these people are (to be checked out). They then went over to Nico's place.
where L-9 joined the family for a Cuban dinner. Nico's mother-in-law was there
she recently came out of Cuba to be with her daughter (Nico's wife) while she
has a baby - due soon. Jorrin appeared soon thereafter and joined in the meal.
Nico put on some popular and light classical records, working his way from
dance music to Tchaikovsky. When a carload of Embassy people -- Rogelio
RODRIGUEZ and wife, Dra. MACHADO, Berta MACHADO, and Buenaventura REYES
appeared in front Nico quickly took off the music and put on a record of
Fidel CASTRO intoning his Second Declaration of Havana - the new arrivals
were greeted with this as they came in the door. L-9 says that Nico is a
superb actor and knew just what to do when the Patris o Muerte types showed
www
7. In response to questioning L-9 revealed that Nico looks upon him as
a Fidelista but definitely not a Communist. He says that Nico is very self
assured, a calm man who cannot be ruffled. He appears to have no complexes
about being a Negro. Asked whether he felt there might be any chance that
Nico would cooperate against CASTRO, L-9 said, "Let us face the fact that
many people are becoming more and more convinced that the revolution is here
to stay. This man GARCIA is one of them. On the other hand, if he could be
"got to" he would be invaluable. He would be a great loss to the Embassy.
I would say that the chances are slim but it would probably be worth the
effort to try to win him over. He has many friends from all walks of life,
many of them among the anti-Castro elements."
8. L-9 showed B some documents regarding Cultural plans of the Embassy
which did not seen to merit reporting. He turned over two long lists of
persons invited to the 2. Jan receptions.
* HOMPSON, an opposition senator from
-->
9. L-9 reported that Mr. Dudley THOMPSON, an opposition senator from
Jamaica had been in town and he identified THOMPSON from among those. photo-
graphed at the Diplomatic Reception of 2 Jan. T was in Nairobi, Kenya, two
weeks ago and arrived in Mexico from Miami on 1 Jan. He hoped to continus
on to Cuba right away but was unable to make the trip since he could not be
he had to be in
assured of getting there and back to Jamaica by 6 Jan
Jamaica on the 6th to attend a meeting of those opposing the BUSTAMANTE
regime and had to attend another meeting on 10 Jan which was to be attended
by Cheddi JAGAN of British Guiana and leaders from Barbados. He hoped to be
able to go to Cuba to see Jesus CANIZARES of the INRA in order to brief C
about land reform measures in Kenya. He told L-9 that he would probably be
back in Mexico in February 1961 to arrange to go to Cuba. L-9 says that T
appears to be a very well educated, bright person.

MEMORANDUM FOR THE RECORD
SECRET
1 January 1964
I
FROM
Lawrence F. Barker
SUBJECT :
Meeting with LITAMIL-9, 6 January 1964
1. A meeting was held with L-9 from 2000 hours until 2320 hours 6
Jan - pick-up and drop-off were made by car, the meeting took place at
Ba home with B's wife working the gate.
--
2. L-9 was unusually depressed had just received a letter from
Spain indicating that his sister had been forced to leave her work as
result of excessive fatigue and the "never ending round of discussions
and study circles" etc. She had not received much sympathy from the
Cuban FOMIN and her request for 2 months leave in Spain was denied pending
further study. L-9, who is quite fond of his sisters, took this news to
heart and it ate away at him and compounded his usual miserable feeling.
The first part of the meeting was taken up in a C/0 delivered pep talk.
L-9 had the following to reports
To $3696
18688
At the evening reception of 2 Jan at the Embassy, the TASS
representative remarked that he believed KHRUSHCHEV did not
travel to Cuba to attend the anniversary celebrations because
of the revelation of an exile plot to bomb Havana revelations
which came about as the result of the arrest by the US Coast
Guard of some war-like Cubans with bombs in their possession
The TASS man said that he believed that KHRUSHCHEV would show
up someday in Havana quite manicunced as did CASTRO in the USSR.'
}
----
--
Teresa PROENZA may be hired back by the Embassy APARICIO
recently remarked to L-9, "Surely they will re-hire her." It
is quite clear that APARICIO doesn't want her in his office again.
and he expressed the wish that if she were to be rehired she
would work in the main embassy building.
In regard to the PROENZA firing, ROJAS of Cubana de Aviacion,
who is married to Teresa's sister, said that he had written to
FOMIN Raul ROA in her behalf but had received no reply.
d. Ambassador HERNANDEZ Armas sent a Christmas present to COROSTIZA
of the Maxican Foreign Office this year -- it was really a New
Year's present, sent 31 Dec. L-9 does not know what it was.
4. L-9 was asked what all the ruckus was at the airport on 5 Jan. This
drew a blank. B then said he had heard that a phalanx of Embassy officers was
out there apparently guarding someone who was on his way to Cuba. L-9 didn't
know anything about it. B remarked that two Cuban officials were supposedly
on the flight to Havana - one from the Embassy in Montevideo. At this point,
L-9 slapped his fomhead and said, "My God, PEREZ! I forgot about him." He then
related the details of a conversation he had had with Earle✓ PEREZ Friman at the
Embassy on 2 Jan - details sent to HQS separately by cable. (See MEXI 7659 ).
L-9 was not aware that PEREZ had been on the 5 Jan flight he described him
perfectly. He was not made aware of KUBARK involvement in the alleged assault”
nor was he told anything about PEREZ' appearance at TPELIDE.
the
--
L-9 identified a number of persons appearing in the photos taken at
plomatic reception held at the Embassy 2 Jan. Identifications were noted

nas.

cuentra en Cuba.

Ovidio Samá, Cónsul en Veracuz, se encuen-

nada le sucederá. 8 cree que mañana jueves
regresará a Veracruz.

DERMITIVE APPRAISAL OF CONTENT IS TENTATIVE
Latin American official in Mexico City who has regular
contact with Cuban Embassy personnel; he has been a reliable.
reporter for about a year and a half. [LITAMIL-9]
-
On 18 January 1964 the Cuban Embassy in Mexico City announced
a three-month plan, according to which certain staff members
will prepare special reports, in addition to their usual
duties. Raul Aparicio Nogales, Consul for Cultural Affairs,
will prepare a report on the Universidad Nacional Autonoma
de Mexico (UNAM National Autonomous University of Mexico),
which will include the physical layout, activities of the
student body, and ways in which the Cuban Government can exert
influence there. Luis Albery Souto, Cultural Attaché, was
instructed to prepare a similar report on the Instituto Nacional
de Bellas Artes (INBA - National Institute of Fine Arts).
Margot Machado Padron, Consul, will prepare a report on countries
which have diplomatic relations with Cuba, emphasizing how
contact with their representatives in Maxico will aid the Castro
Government. Rogelio Rodriguez Lopes, Second Secretary, was
given an assignment as Political Reporting Officer.

SUBJECT
Shipment of Explosives to
Mexico
DATE DISTR 25 August 1964
NO. PAGES
1
REFERENCES.

DATE OF

DATE ACQAugust 1964
FIELD REPORT NO.
THIS IS UNEVALUATED INFORMATION SOURCE GRADINGS ARE DEFINITIVE APPRAISAL OF CONTENT IS TENTATIVE
SOURCE: A former Cuban IS officer who served with the Cuban Intelligence
Service until April 1964.
Following is a translation of a report which source
wrote concerning a shipment of explosives to Mexico:
"The Communist Party of El Salvador had asked me to
send them twenty-five, one quarter pound packages of
gelatin explosives. They requested that the explosives be
sent to Mexico where they would recover them and take
them to El Salvador.
"In view of the request, I spoke with Manuel PINEIRO
regarding the shipment itself, as well as the amount.
PINEIRO answered by telling me to do so.
"During my trip to Mexico (March 1964) I spoke with
Rogelio RODRIGUEZ Lopez regarding this shipment and he told
me that there was no need of my sending the explosives
to Mexico as this type of explosive was available in the
Embassy. I then told RODRIGUEZ that I would answer the
request from El Salvador.
"Upon returning to Cuba I spoke with PINEIRO, who told
me not to send the explosives as the orders now were to
send nothing but money due to the recent exposure of the
arms shipment to Venezuela."

This document is for the use of your

Reference is made to your communication of
May 26, 1964, that the subject and his chauffeur planned
to travel to Nuevo Laredo to pick up a new automobile.
A confidential source, who has furnished
reliable information in the past, furnished the follow-
ing information on July 24, 1964:
ROGELIO RODRIGUEZ, of 160 Uturgas Street,
Mexico City, was in Nuevo Laredo on May 27, 1964, to
obtain an automobile for the Cuban Embassy in Mexico
City. A 1964 black Ford Galaxie 500, Serial Number
4B62x150451, was delivered to RODRIGUEZ on May 27, 1964.
RODRIGUEZ appeared to be about 23 years of age,
and it is known that he was buying cigarettes and radios
during his stay in Nuevo Laredo.

A. UPON HEARING THAT UNCLE AND AUNT SERIOUSLY ILL, SUBJ
SUBJ
LEFT BY PLANE VIA MEXICO CITY TO LIMA, ARRIVING 6 SEPT 63.
UNCLE ERNESTO VELARDE DIED OCTOBER 63, AUNT ELENA ARENAS DE
VELARDE DIED 3 DEC 63. ON HIS PARENTS URGING
ON HIS PARENTS URGING, SUBJ WROTE PRES
KENNEDY IMMEDIATELY ON ARRIVAL LIMA. NOV 63 RECEIVED REPLY
VIA COL BENSON, MILATT AT LIMA. HOWEVER DID NOT SEE COL BENSON
UNTIL FEBRUARY OR MARCH 64.
B. JANUARY 64 SUBJ ACCIDENTALLY NET LONGTIME FRIEND
ERNESTO AYZA DEL RISCO, DOB CA 38, SPANISH CIT. SURJ FIRST
DISCOVERED THAT AYZA INVOLVED WITH COMMUNISTS IN MARCH 63 WHILE
SUBJ WAS VISITING PERU. AT THAT TIME A LIMA POLICEMAN WAS RUN
OVER AND KILLED BY SECRETARY GENERAL OF PERUVIAN YOUNG COMMUNIST
GROUP WHO WAS DRIVING CAR OWNED BY AYZA. AYZA SUGGESTED SUBJ NOT
RETURN U.S. BUT GO CUBA INSTEAD AND INTRODUCED SUBJ TO RENTERIA
WHO "WOULD ARRANGE EVERYTHING.'
C. BETWEEN JANUARY AND MARCH, SUBJ SAW RENTERIA APPROXIMATELY
EVERY TWO WEEKS. AT EACH MEETING RENTERIA CLAIMED PLANS TO GO
TO CUBA WERE PROGRESSING. DURING THIS PERIOD SUBJ THOUGHT
RENTERIA "JUST MAKING TALK". HOWEVER IN MARCH RENTERIA
ANNOUNCED PLANS COMPLETED, AND THEY READY TO GO. THEN INTRODUCED
SUBJECT TO CASTRO LAVARELLO, SALOMON BOLO HIDALGO AND GENERAL PANDO.
D. SUBJ AND RENTERIA TRAVELLED TOGETHER TO MEXICO CITY ARRIVING
1. APRIL. RENTERIA CARRIED SEALED. LETTER FROM LAVARELLO TO "SENOR
JORDAN" WHICH RENTERIA WAS TO DELIVER AT CURAN EMBASSY MEXICO. AT
THIS POINT IN INTERVIEW, SUBJECT VOLUNTEERED ADDITIONAL INFORMATION
ON JORDAN: JORDAN IS G-2 OFFICER. SUBJ BELIEVES THAT JORDAN IS
MAN IN CHARGE OF CUBAN PROGRAM TO TRAIN OTHER LATIN AMERICAN
NATIONALS IN SUBVERSION AND GUERILLA WARFARE. SINCE SUBJ AT NO
TIME IN CUBA WAS IN COMPANY OF OTHER THAN PERUVIANS, THIS IS LOGICAL
MISUNDERSTANDING. SUBJ MET JORDAN ON SEVERAL OCCASIONS. HOWEVER
JORDAN HELD SUBSTANTIVE DISCUSSIONS ONLY WITH RENTERIA WHO, DURING
ENTIRE TIME AND ON ALL. MATTERS, WAS CONSIDERED SUBJ SUPERVISOR AND
HANDLER. SUBJ PAID OWN FARE. FROM LIMA TO MEXICO. GEN PANDO,
THROUGH LAVARELLO, GAVE RENTERIA AND SURJ EACH 2000 SOLES POČKET

WHO "WOULD ARRANCE EVERYTHING."

ANNOUNCED PLANS COMPLETED, AND THEY READY TO GO. THEN INTRODUCED

1. Rogelio RODRIGUEZ Lopez, who uses the pseudonyms "Eduardo,
'"Casimiro," and "Jose Antonio," is an officer of the
Direccion General de Inteligencia (DGI - General Directorate
of Intelligence) stationed in Mexico City, Mexico.
RODRIGUEZ, who was born in approximately 1940, is five
feet eight inches tall, has a husky build, a reddish
1 complexion and blond hair. 1,2,3,4,5,6,7

third secretary of the Cuban Embassy in Mexico City.
Source also said that RODRIGUEZ had plans to see
Major Alfonso PRERA, leader of the 13 November Group
in Mexico on 24 March 1962.
:
In a report dated 14 February 1964 Rogelio RODRIGUEZ
Lopez was reported to be the second secretary of the
Cuban Embassy in Mexico City.

MAR 22 3 55 PH *65
A fairly reliable source in a document dated 4 March 1964
said that Rogelio RODRIGUEZ, at the 18 January 1964 Cuban
Embassy staff meeting, was given the assignment as Political
Reporting Officer.
In a report dated 26 April 1964 it was reported that Rogelio
RODRIGUEZ Lopez, second secretary of the Cuban Embassy in
Mexico City, uses the pseudonyms "Chele" and "Gorrin with
his contacts in Mexico.
On 28 April 1964 it was reported that Rogelio RODRIGUEZ, a
known Cuban intelligence service officer, left Mexico for
Cuba on 25 April 1964 for a permanent change of station.
In the 17 May 1964 issue of Hoy it was reported that Rogelio
RODRIGUEZ Lopez, second secretary of the Cuban Embassy in
Mexico City, left Cuba on 16 May 1964 to return to duty in
Mexico.
A fairly reliable source in a report dated 5 June 1964 stated
that Rogelio RODRIGUEZ, second secretary of the Cuban Embassy
in Mexico City, is the son of a Communist Party member and
that he (RODRIGUEZ) previously worked in the Foreign Office
on Mexican matters in the Latin American Political
Department. Source also said that he thought RODRIGUEZ
probably worked for Manuėl PINEIRO.

EXCERPT
DST-11954
27 June 1964
FROM : Amembassy MEXICO
SUBJECT: Changes in Soviet Bloc Diplomatic Personnel in Mexico
The Mexico City daily Excelsior reported on June 17 that Rogelio
RODRIGUEZ Lopez, Second Secretary of the Cuban Embassy, was given a
farewell party by his friends. Rodriguez recently made a trip to
Cuba and, at that time, it was rumored that he would be transferred.
Instead, he returned to Mexico. The Embassy possesses no other
information regarding Rodriguez' possible re-assignment.
For the Charge d'Affaires ad interim:
Wallace W. Stuart
Counselor of Embassy
for Political Affairs

series containing personality information provided by the
source and includes supplemental information from the
records of this Agency.

Rogelio RODRIGUEZ Lopez, who uses the pseudonyms "Eduardo,"
"Casimiro, " and "Jose Antonio, " is an officer of the
Direccion General de Inteligencia (DGI General Directorate
of Intelligence) stationed in Mexico City, Mexico.
-
RODRIGUEZ, who was born in approximately 1940, is five
feet eight inches tall, has a husky build, a reddish
complexion and blond hair. 1,2,3,4,5,6,7
Headquarters Comments.
1.
2
A usually reliable source in a report dated 29 March
1962 stated that Rogelio RODRIGUEZ Lopez is the
third secretary of the Cuban Embassy in Mexico City.
Source also said that RODRIGUEZ had plans to see
Major Alfonso PRERA, leader of the 13 November Group
in Mexico on 24 March 1962.
2. In a report dated 14 February 1964 Rogelio RODRIGUEZ
Lopez was reported to be the second secretary of the
Cuban Embassy in Mexico City.
